Five Types of the Prophet's Intercession
Lists five types of intercession with rulings on exclusivity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five types of intercession of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and the scholarly rulings on whether each is exclusive to him or shared.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession has five distinct types, and not all are exclusive to him.

In this passage from the Sharh al-'Aqida al-Tahawiyya, Imam al-Maydani enumerates the five types of shafa'a (intercession) granted to the Prophet. He clarifies which types are uniquely his and which are shared with other prophets and believers, addressing differences of opinion among scholars. This classification is essential for a proper understanding of the Prophet's role on the Day of Resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to get an overview of the five types.
Notice the detailed description of the first type (Great Intercession) and the concise treatment of the others.
2
Identify the first type (Great Intercession)
Focus on the first type: the intercession for relief from the terrors of the Day of Resurrection. Note that it is exclusive to the Prophet and unanimously accepted.
This type is the greatest and most comprehensive.
3
Examine the remaining four types
Go through types 2-5. For each, note the description and the scholars' positions on exclusivity. Pay attention to where there is consensus and where there is disagreement.
Some types are exclusive, some are not, and some have differing opinions.
4
Reflect on the pattern of exclusivity
Consider the overall pattern: not all intercession is exclusive to the Prophet. The passage shows that some intercessions are shared with other prophets and believers.
This corrects a common misunderstanding that all intercession is unique to the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحدها - وهي أعظمها وأعمها شفاعته عليه الصلاة والسلام بعد أن يكلم الناس الأنبياء حين يعاينون من شدائد الموقف وأهواله وطول القيام فيه لرب العالمين وزيادة القلق وتصاعد العرق ما يذيب الأكباد وينسي الأولاد مدة ثلاثة آلاف سنة؛ فيترادُّونها من آدم إلى عيسى في خمسة آلاف سنة أيضًا؛ إذ بين سؤال كل نبي وآخر ألف سنة - كما قال ابن حجر والقرطبي وغيرهما - فإذا انتهوا إليه صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «أَنَا هَا أَنَا لَهَا أُمَّتِي أُمني، وكل من قبله لا يقول إلا : نفسي ،نفسي اذهبوا إلى غيري، وهذه مختصة به وتسمى الشفاعة العظمى، وهذه مجمع عليها لم ينكرها أحد ممن يقول بالحشر؛ إذ هي للإراحة من طول الوقوف حين يتمنون الانصراف من موقفهم ولو إلى النار.

وثانيها: في إدخال قوم الجنة بغير حساب، وهذه أيضًا خاصة به على ما قاله القاضي والنووي، وتردد ابن دقيق العيد في الاختصاص، وتبعه ابن حجر قائلا: لا دليل عليه، وقد ذكر حديثها مسلم.

وثالثها: في قوم استوجبوا النار فيشفع هم فلا يدخلونها، وهذه جزم القاضي وابن السبكي بعدم اختصاصها به، وتردد النووي.

ورابعها فيمن دخل النار من المؤمنين المذنبين، وهذه وقع إطباق القوم على عدم اختصاصها به

وخامسها الشفاعة في رفع الدرجات في الجنة، وهذه لا ينكرها أيضًا المعتزلة كالأولى ... إلى أن قال: وقد بقيت شفاعات أخر وردت بها آثار لا تخلو عن مقال
The first – and it is the greatest and most comprehensive – is his intercession, peace and blessings be upon him, after the people speak to the prophets when they witness from the severities of the standing and its terrors and the length of standing therein for the Lord of the worlds and increased anxiety and rising sweat what melts livers and makes one forget children for a period of three thousand years; so they pass it from Adam to Jesus over five thousand years as well; for between the request of each prophet and another is a thousand years – as Ibn Hajar and al-Qurtubi and others said – so when they end at him, peace and blessings be upon him, he says: 'I am, I am for it, my community, my community', and everyone before him says only: 'myself, myself, go to other than me'. And this is exclusive to him and is called the Great Intercession, and this is agreed upon, not denied by anyone who affirms the Resurrection; for it is for relief from the length of standing when they wish to depart from their station even to the Fire.

The second: concerning the admission of a people into Paradise without account, and this is also exclusive to him according to what al-Qadi and al-Nawawi said, and Ibn Daqiq al-'Id hesitated about its exclusivity, and Ibn Hajar followed him saying: there is no evidence for it, and Muslim has mentioned its hadith.

The third: concerning a people who have deserved the Fire, so he intercedes for them and they do not enter it, and this – al-Qadi and Ibn al-Subki definitively stated its non-exclusivity to him, and al-Nawawi hesitated.

The fourth: concerning those who have entered the Fire from among the sinful believers, and this – the community has agreed on its non-exclusivity to him.

The fifth: intercession for raising ranks in Paradise, and this is also not denied by the Mu'tazila like the first... until he said: and there remain other intercessions reported by traditions that are not free from discussion.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration and classification of the types of intercession (shafa'a) of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) by Imam al-Maydani in his commentary on al-'Aqida al-Tahawiyya. The author lists five types, each with its own ruling regarding whether it is exclusive to the Prophet or shared with other prophets or believers.

The first type is the Great Intercession (al-shafa'a al-'uzma) for the people to be judged and relieved from the terrors of the Day of Resurrection. This is the greatest and most comprehensive, as the prophets themselves seek it, finally ending with the Prophet Muhammad, who declares his readiness for his community. This intercession is exclusive to him and unanimously accepted by those who affirm the Resurrection.

The second type is intercession for admitting a group of people into Paradise without any prior account or punishment. According to al-Qadi 'Iyad and al-Nawawi, this too is exclusive to the Prophet, though Ibn Daqiq al-'Id and Ibn Hajar questioned that exclusivity due to lack of clear evidence, noting that Muslim recorded a hadith about it.

The third type is intercession for people who have deserved the Fire but are spared from entering it through his intercession. Here, al-Qadi 'Iyad and Ibn al-Subki definitively stated that this intercession is not exclusive to the Prophet, while al-Nawawi hesitated on the matter.

The fourth type is intercession for sinful believers who have already entered the Fire, to be brought out from it. The consensus of the scholars (ijma') is that this intercession is not exclusive to the Prophet; other prophets and righteous believers may also intercede.

The fifth type is intercession for raising the ranks of believers in Paradise. This is not denied even by the Mu'tazila, just like the first type. The author then notes that there remain other types of intercession reported in traditions, but these are subject to scholarly discussion and not free from differing opinions.

Thus, the passage clarifies the scope and authority of the Prophet's intercession, distinguishing between types that are exclusive to him and those that are shared.

Key Terms
شفاعة
الشفاعة العظمى
اختصاص
إطباق القوم
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All types of intercession are exclusive to the Prophet.
Correction: Some types, like intercession for sinful believers who entered the Fire and intercession for raising ranks, are not exclusive according to scholarly consensus or majority.

Checkpoint
Which type of intercession did the Mu'tazila also affirm, according to the passage?
A) The Great Intercession for relief from the standing
B) Intercession for entering Paradise without account
C) Intercession for raising ranks in Paradise
D) Intercession for those who deserved the Fire

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's intercession encompasses multiple types, with the Great Intercession and others being exclusive to him, while intercession for sinners and raising ranks is shared.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the Prophet said 'my community, my community' while others said 'myself, myself', you see a selfless love that sacrificed even his own comfort. In your daily interactions, do you find yourself thinking 'myself' more often than 'my community'? What is one concrete habit you can change today to put others before yourself, even when it costs you something?
?
The Great Intercession is a hope for every believer, but it is based on affirming the Resurrection and trusting in the Prophet's promise. Is your hope in that intercession built on a deep, active faith—or is it a passive assumption that guarantees salvation? What will you study or practice this week to make your hope more certain and your actions more aligned with that hope?
?
Even the Mu'tazila admitted intercession for raising ranks in Paradise. This shows how vast Allah's mercy is—He elevates His servants through the Prophet's plea. Are you content with just entering Paradise, or are you actively seeking higher ranks? What deed can you perform today that would make you long for elevation, not just escape from punishment?

The Covenant of Adam's Offspring: A Real Event in a Single Moment
Al-Taftazani cites an exegetical view on the mithaq from al-Talwih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the interpretive view that the taking of the covenant (mithaq) occurred in a single, instantaneous moment, with all offspring extracted from Adam, given form, speech, and then returned and made to forget.

Core Idea
The mithaq was a real, momentary event where all humans acknowledged Allah.

Al-Taftazani, in his commentary al-Talwih, presents a striking interpretation of the well-known mithaq verse. A group of exegetes understood the extraction of Adam's offspring and the taking of the covenant as a literal, instantaneous occurrence, analogous to the resurrection. This passage outlines that view, emphasizing the trial of forgetfulness and faith in the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the two key events: the extraction of offspring and the taking of the covenant.
The passage is a quotation from al-Talwih.
2
Examine the analogy with the trumpet blasts
The exegetes compare the extraction to the two trumpet blasts that cause death and resurrection. This emphasizes that the entire process occurred in an instant.
The analogy underscores the miraculous nature of the event.
3
Reflect on the purpose of forgetfulness
Why did Allah cause us to forget? The text says it is a trial so that we believe in the unseen. Consider how this tests faith.
Forgetfulness does not negate the reality of the event.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذهب جمع من المفسرين إلى أن الله تعالى أخرج ذرية آدم بعضهم من بعض على حسب ما يتوالدون إلى يوم القيامة في أدنى مدة كموت الكل بالنفخ في الصور وحياة الكل بالنفخة الثانية؛ فصورهم واستنطقهم وأخذ ميثاقهم ثم أعادهم في صلب آدم ثم أنسانا تلك الحالة ابتلاء لنؤمن بالغيب.
A group of exegetes held that Allah the Exalted extracted the offspring of Adam, some from others, according to how they procreate until the Day of Resurrection, in the shortest duration, like the death of all with the blast of the Trumpet and the life of all with the second blast; He formed them, made them speak, took their covenant, then returned them to the loins of Adam, then made us forget that state as a trial so that we believe in the unseen.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from al-Talwih by al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani), presenting an interpretation of the taking of the covenant (mithaq) from Adam's offspring. It states that a group of exegetes hold that Allah extracted all human offspring from Adam in a single, brief moment, analogous to the two trumpet blasts that cause universal death and resurrection. In that instant, Allah gave them form, speech, and took their covenant of recognition and obedience, then returned them to Adam's loins and caused them to forget that event. This forgetfulness serves as an ordeal to test faith in the unseen.

Key Terms
ميثاق
ذرية آدم
النفخ في الصور
الغيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the mithaq is merely metaphorical and did not literally happen.
Correction: This passage affirms that a group of exegetes held it to be a literal event.

Key Takeaway
A group of exegetes affirmed the mithaq as a literal, real event in which all humans acknowledged Allah in an instant, then were made to forget as a test of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What one step will you take today to live by that unseen pledge?
?

Belief in the Preserved Tablet and the Pen
Imam Maydani affirms belief in the Preserved Tablet and the Pen as created entities, citing Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Preserved Tablet and the Pen are real created entities through which Allah's decree is recorded and fixed, and that Muslims must affirm them based on revelation.

Core Idea
The Pen has dried — nothing can change what Allah has written.

Imam al-Maydani continues his exposition of the articles of faith by turning to two specific created entities: the Preserved Tablet and the Pen. These are not metaphors but real, luminous bodies through which Allah records all that will occur. This lesson establishes the Sunni doctrine of their reality and the finality of the divine decree inscribed upon them.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify the core belief
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the opening phrase 'We believe in the Tablet and the Pen' – this is a direct statement of faith.
2
Understand the Pen's drying
The phrase 'The Pen has dried' means that every event until the Day of Resurrection is already written and cannot be altered. Consider the implications for human free will and trust in Allah's decree.
3
Examine the descriptions
Both are described as 'great luminous bodies.' Note the hadith that elaborates on the Tablet's appearance and the Pen's function. Reflect on why these descriptions are important for tawhid.
The hadith from Ibn Umar is incomplete in this passage.

Source Text

وَنُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّوْحِ وَالقَلَمِ بِجَمِيعِ مَا فِيهِ قَدْ رُقِمَ؛ فَلَوِ اجْتَمَعَ الخَلْقُ كُلُّهُمْ عَلَى شَيْءٍ كتبهُ اللهُ فِيهِ أَنَّهُ كَائِنُ لِيَجْعَلُوهُ غَيْرَ كَائِن لَمْ يَقْدِرُوا عَلَيْهِ؛ جَفَّ القَلَمُ بِمَا هُوَ كَائِنُ إِلَى يَوْمِ القِيَامَةِ.
ونؤمن باللوح المحفوظ، وهو جسم عظيم نوراني كتب فيه القلم بإذن الله تعالى ما هو كائن إلى يوم القيامة، ( والقلم ) وهو جسم عظيم نوراني خلقه تعالى من نوره؛ فنؤمن بأنهما مخلوقان الله تعالى موجودان ثابتان كما وردت به الآيات القرآنية والأحاديث النبوية؛ قال تعالى: في لوح محفوظ) [سورة البروج آية: ٢٢] وقال: ﴿ن وَالْقَلَمِ وَمَا يَسْطُرُونَ ﴾ [سورة القلم آية: ١]، وفي الهيئة السنية للجلال السيوطي أخرج أبو الشيخ (۱) من طريق مالك بن دينار (۲) عن أنس قال: قال رسول الله : «إِنَّ الله لَوْحًا أَحَدُ وَجْهَيهِ يَاقُونَةٌ عَمْرَاءُ وَالوَجْهُ الثَّانِي زُمُرُّدَةٌ خَضْرَاءُ فَلَمُهُ النُّورُ فِيهِ يَخْلُقُ وَفِيهِ يَرْزُقُ وَفِيهِ يُحْيِي وَفِيهِ يُمِيتُ وَفِيهِ يُعِزُّ وَفِيهِ يَفْعَلُ مَا يَشَاءُ فِي كُل يَومٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ (۳). وأخرج أبو الشيخ عن ابن عمر له عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «إِنَّ اللهَ أَوَّلُ شَيْءٍ خَلَقَ
And we believe in the Tablet and the Pen, and in all that is inscribed therein. So if all of creation gathered together to make something that Allah had written in it as existing into non-existence, they would not be able to do so. The Pen has dried regarding what is to be until the Day of Resurrection. And we believe in the Preserved Tablet (al-Lawh al-Mahfuz), and it is a great luminous body in which the Pen wrote, by the permission of Allah Most High, whatever is to be until the Day of Resurrection. And (the Pen) is a great luminous body that He created from His light. So we believe that both are created by Allah Most High, existing and established, as has come in the Qur'anic verses and prophetic hadith. He said, 'In a preserved tablet' (Surah al-Buruj 22) and said, 'Nun. By the pen and what they inscribe' (Surah al-Qalam 1). And in al-Hay'a al-Sunniyya by al-Jalal al-Suyuti, Abu al-Shaykh narrated from Malik ibn Dinar from Anas who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Indeed, Allah has a tablet, one of its two faces is a red ruby and the second face is a green emerald; its pen is light; in it He creates, in it He provides, in it He gives life, in it He causes death, in it He exalts, and in it He does whatever He wills every day and night.' And Abu al-Shaykh narrated from Ibn 'Umar from the Prophet, peace be upon him, who said: 'Indeed, the first thing Allah created...'
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage affirms the orthodox Sunni belief in the Preserved Tablet (al-Lawh al-Mahfuz) and the Pen (al-Qalam) as real created entities. The author begins with a statement of belief: we believe in the Tablet and the Pen and all that is inscribed therein. He then emphasizes the decisiveness of what is written: if all creatures together tried to change something Allah has written as existing into non-existence, they could not; the Pen has dried (jaffa al-qalam) concerning all that will happen until the Day of Resurrection, meaning divine predestination is fixed. Next, he describes the Preserved Tablet as a great luminous body (jism 'azim nurani) into which the Pen wrote, by Allah's permission, everything that will occur until the Last Day. The Pen is also described as a great luminous body created by Allah from His light. Both are created, existing, and established, as proven by the Quranic verses and prophetic hadith. He cites two Quranic proofs: Surah al-Buruj 22 ("in a preserved tablet") and Surah al-Qalam 1 ("Nun. By the pen and what they inscribe"). He then quotes a hadith from Abu al-Shaykh on the authority of Malik ibn Dinar from Anas, describing the Tablet as having two faces: one of red ruby and the other of green emerald, and its pen is light; through it Allah creates, provides, gives life, causes death, exalts, and does whatever He wills every day and night. Finally, he begins another hadith (incomplete) from Abu al-Shaykh from Ibn 'Umar that the first thing Allah created was... (the text cuts off). This passage reinforces that the Tablet and Pen are part of the unseen realities that Muslims must accept on the basis of revelation.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Tablet and Pen are mere metaphors or symbols, not real physical objects.
Correction: The passage affirms they are actual created bodies (ajsam nuraniyya) as described in the Quran and hadith.

Checkpoint
What does the expression 'جف القلم' (the Pen has dried) signify in this passage?
A) The Pen is no longer writing.
B) The Pen has broken and cannot write.
C) The decrees have been finalized and are unchangeable.
D) The Pen is made of dried ink.

Key Takeaway
The Preserved Tablet and the Pen are real, created, luminous bodies through which Allah's unchangeable decree is recorded, and believing in them is part of iman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe the Pen has dried and nothing can change what Allah has written about your life, why do you still worry about the future? How does this belief challenge your daily anxiety?
?
The hadith describes the Tablet as the means through which Allah creates, provides, gives life, and causes death. How does understanding that your entire existence is recorded in a tablet affect your sense of control over your own life?
?
You are told that even if all creation conspired to change one thing Allah has decreed, they could not. In what area of your life do you still act as if you can override Allah's decree through your own effort? What would it take for you to surrender that area completely to Him?

The Reality of the Throne and Chair
Affirmation of the Throne and Chair with definition and transmitted description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Throne and Chair are real created entities, that Allah is independent of them and encompasses all, and the definition of the Throne as a great luminous celestial body while acknowledging our limited knowledge.

Core Idea
The Throne and Chair are true, but Allah is independent and beyond spatial containment.

This passage from the Sharh al-Tahawiyyah affirms the reality of the Throne and Chair as created entities, while emphasizing Allah's absolute independence and encompassing power. It also provides a definition of the Throne and transmits a descriptive tradition, reminding us that its exact reality is beyond our knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the three key affirmations: the reality of Throne and Chair, Allah's independence, and His encompassing.
2
Identify the definition of the Throne
Find al-Laqqani's definition and note the qualification that we have no definitive knowledge of its reality.
The definition is 'a great luminous celestial body encompassing all bodies'.
3
Examine the transmitted report
Read the report from Wahb ibn Munabbih and understand that it is illustrative, not a matter of creedal certainty.
The commentator does not assert this as definitive.
4
Reflect on the core teaching
Ask yourself: What does this passage teach about Allah's relationship to the Throne? It teaches independence and encompassing, not spatial location.
This connects to avoiding anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالعرش والكرسي
وَالْعَرْشُ وَالْكُرْسِيُّ حَقٌّ، وَهُوَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ مُسْتَغْنٍ عَنِ الْعَرْشِ وَمَا دُونَهُ، مُحِيطٌ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ وَبِمَا فَوْقَهُ وَقَدْ أَعْجَزَ عَنِ الإِحَاطَةِ خَلْقَهُ.
(و) نقول: (العرش) وهو في اللغة السرير، ومعناه هنا كما قال اللقاني: هو جسم عظيم نوراني علوي محيط بجميع الأجسام، قيل: هو أول المخلوقات وجودًا عينيا، ولا قطع لنا بتعيين حقيقته لعدم العلم بها (١)، وإن أخرج ابن أبي حاتم (٢) في تفسيره وأبو الشيخ في كتاب العظمة عن وهب بن منبه (٣) قال: «إن الله خلق العرش من نوره والكرسي بالعرش ملتصق والماء كله في جوف الكرسي والماء على متن الريح، وحول العرش أربعة أنهار: نهر من نور يتلألأ ونهر من نار تتلظى ونهر من ثلج أبيض تلتمع منه الأبصار ونهر من ماء والملائكة قيام في تلك الأنهار يسبحون الله تعالى، وللعرش ألسنة بعدد ألسنة الخلق كلهم يسبح الله تعالى ويذكره بتلك الألسنة».
(١) هداية المريد ص (٣٥٧).
(٢) عبدالرحمن بن أبي حاتم محمد بن إدريس بن المنذر، أبو محمد التميمي الحنظلي، الإمام الحافظ الناقد، كان بحرًا في العلوم ومعرفة الرجال ثقة حافظا زاهدًا، من مصنفاته: الجرح والتعديل والتفسير والرد على الجهمية، توفي سنة ٣٢٧هـ.
(٣) وهب بن منبه بن كامل اليماني الصنعاني، أبو عبدالله الأبناوي، الإمام الأخباري من التابعين الثقات، ولد في زمن عثمان له ورحل وحج وأخذ عن الصحابة، وروايته للمتقدم قليلة وإنما غزارة علمه في الإسرائيليات وصحائف أهل الكتاب، توفي سنة ١١٤هـ.
(٤) انظر: العظمة (٥٤٣/٢-٥٤٤)، وتفسير ابن أبي حاتم عند قوله تعالى: "ثم استوى على العرش يغشي الليل النهار" [سورة الأعراف آية: ٥٤].
Belief in the Throne and the Chair. And the Throne and the Chair are true, and He, Mighty and Majestic, is independent of the Throne and what is below it, encompassing everything and what is above it, and He has incapacitated His creation from encompassing it. (And) we say: the Throne – which in language is a bed, and its meaning here as al-Laqqani said: it is a great luminous celestial body encompassing all bodies; it is said: it is the first of created things in terms of specific existence, and we have no definitive determination of its reality due to lack of knowledge of it. And indeed Ibn Abi Hatim in his Tafsir and Abu al-Shaykh in Kitab al-‘Azamah narrated from Wahb ibn Munabbih who said: 'Allah created the Throne from His light, and the Chair is attached to the Throne, and all water is in the cavity of the Chair, and the water is on the back of the wind, and around the Throne are four rivers: a river of light shining, a river of fire blazing, a river of white snow from which eyes dazzle, and a river of water; and the angels are standing in those rivers glorifying Allah Most High, and the Throne has tongues equal to the number of tongues of all creation, each glorifying Allah Most High and remembering Him with those tongues.' Footnotes: (1) Hidayah al-Murid p. 357. (2) Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Hatim... (3) Wahb ibn Munabbih... (4) See: al-‘Azamah 2/543-544, and Tafsir Ibn Abi Hatim at His saying: 'Then He established Himself over the Throne, covering the night with the day.'
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Tahawiyyah statement regarding belief in the Throne (al-‘arsh) and the Chair (al-kursi). The Tahawiyyah text affirms that the Throne and the Chair are true (ḥaqq), meaning they are real existent entities. It then clarifies that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, is independent of the Throne and everything beneath it; He encompasses all things, including what is above the Throne, yet He has rendered His creation incapable of fully encompassing Him—or possibly the Throne. The commentator then provides a definition of the Throne: linguistically it means a bed, but in this context, following al-Laqqani, it is defined as a great luminous celestial body that encompasses all other bodies. There is a view that it is the first created thing in terms of specific existence, but we cannot definitively determine its reality because we lack certain knowledge of it. The commentator then transmits a lengthy report from Wahb ibn Munabbih (through Ibn Abi Hatim and Abu al-Shaykh) describing the Throne's creation from Allah's light, the Chair's attachment to it, the water inside the Chair, the four rivers around the Throne, the angels standing in them, and the Throne having tongues equal to the number of all creation's tongues that glorify Allah. This report is included to illustrate the nature of the Throne, though the commentator notes that its exact reality is not definitively known. The footnotes provide source references and brief biographies of Ibn Abi Hatim (a hadith critic and scholar) and Wahb ibn Munabbih (a Tabi‘i known for Isra’iliyyat), as well as a citation for the report.

الكرسي
حق
استغناء
إحاطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah is physically located on the Throne.
Correction: The passage affirms the Throne is a created entity and that Allah is independent of it and encompasses it, negating any spatial relationship.

Checkpoint

B) A great luminous celestial body encompassing all bodies
C) The same as the Chair
D) An abstract concept beyond human knowledge

Key Takeaway
The Throne and Chair are real created entities, but Allah is independent of them, and we affirm their existence without claiming full knowledge of their nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that we affirm the reality of the Throne without claiming full knowledge of its nature. Are there matters of the unseen about which you have insisted on unnecessary details or mental images, rather than submitting to Allah's wisdom in keeping them unknown? How can you train yourself to hold back from excessive speculation?
?
The lesson emphasizes that Allah is independent of the Throne and all of creation. Do your daily worries and anxieties reflect a belief in Allah's absolute independence and control, or do you sometimes act as if your problems are beyond His reach? What would change in your life if you truly internalized that Allah is completely independent and encompasses everything?
?
Consider your language when speaking about Allah's attributes. Do you ever unintentionally imply that Allah is confined to a place, even in subtle ways? This lesson reminds us that even the Throne, the greatest creation, does not contain Him. How can you guard your tongue and heart from any form of spatial limitation when thinking of Allah?

The Kursi and Its Relation to the Throne
Describes the Kursi and its relation to the Throne using Quran, hadith, and angelic descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic description of the Kursi (Footstool) of Allah, its angelic carriers, and its relationship to the Throne (Arsh) as conveyed in the Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
The Kursi is vast, but the Throne is far greater—a reminder of Allah's infinite majesty.

This passage from the Sharh al-Tahawiyyah provides a detailed description of the Kursi (Footstool) of Allah, including its size, its angelic carriers, and its relationship to the Throne. The famous hadith of Abu Dharr uses a powerful analogy to illustrate the relative scale: the seven heavens compared to the Kursi are like a ring in a desert, and the Throne surpasses the Kursi by an even greater margin. Let's explore this awe-inspiring teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the translation. Let the descriptions of the Kursi and Throne sink in before analyzing.
Focus on the hadith analogy and the description of the four angels.
2
Understand the description of the Kursi
Identify the key features: the Kursi is under the Throne, each pillar spans the seven heavens and earths, and it is carried by four angels with four faces each.
The angels petition for provision for different creatures.
3
Analyze the hadith of Abu Dharr
Examine the Prophet's analogy: the heavens relative to the Kursi are like a ring in a desert, and the Throne's superiority over the Kursi is like that desert over the ring. Understand the scale.
This shows the immense size of the Kursi and the even greater size of the Throne.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
Consider why these descriptions matter: they affirm Allah's absolute greatness and the reality of these creations, countering those who deny or misinterpret them.
The passage ends by affirming that both are true, established by Quran and hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكُرْسِيُّ كَفَضْلِ الفَلَاةِ عَلَى تِلْكَ الحَلْقَةِ، وأخرج ابن جرير عن الضحاك قال: الكرسي الذي يوضع تحت العرش الذي يجعل الملوك عليه أقدامهم، وأخرج الفريابي وابن المنذر وابن أبي حاتم والحاكم في المستدرك وصححه على شرط الشيخين عن ابن عباس قال: الكرسي موضع القدمين، والعرش لا يقدر أحد قدره، كذا ذكره اللقاني. وفي رشف النصائح للسهروردي رحمه الله تعالى قال: ومما ورد من عظيم قدرة الله تعالى وخلقه الذي تتضاءل دون إدراكه العقول وتتلاشى الأفهام في وصف الكرسي يقول الله تعالى: ﴿وَسِعَ كُرْسِيُّهُ السَّمَواتِ وَالْأَرْضَ﴾ [سورة البقرة آية: ٢٥٥] - ورد أن كل قائمة من الكرسي طولها مثل السموات السبع والأرضين السبع، وهو بين يدي العرش ويحمل الكرسي بأربعة أملاك لكل ملك أربعة وجوه أقدامهم في الصخرة التي تحت الأرض السابعة السفلى خمسمائة عام، ملك على صورة سيد البشر آدم عليه السلام وهو يسأل للآدميين الرزق والمطر من السنة إلى السنة، وملك على صورة سيد الأنعام وهو الثور يسأل للأنعام الرزق من السنة إلى السنة، وملك على صورة سيد السباع وهو الأسد يسأل للسباع الرزق من السنة إلى السنة، وملك على صورة سيد الطير وهو النسر يسأل للطير الرزق من السنة إلى السنة، وعن أبي إدريس الخولاني عن أبي ذر قال: قلت: يا رسول الله أي آية نزل عليك أعظم؟ قال: «آيَةُ الكُرْسِيِّ»، ثم قال: «يَا أَبَا ذَر مَا السَّمَوَاتُ السَّبْعُ مَعَ الكُرْسِيِّ إِلَّا كَحَلْقَةٍ مُلْقَاةٍ بِأَرْضِ فَلَاةٍ وَفَضْلُ العَرْشِ عَلَى الكُرْسِيِّ كَفَضْلِ الفَلَاةِ عَلَى الحَلْقَةِ»، وفي بعض الأخبار: إن بين حملة العرش وحملة الكرسي سبعون حجابًا من ظلمة وسبعون حجابًا من نور، غلظ كل حجاب مسيرة خمسمائة سنة؛ ولولا ذلك لاحترقت حملة الكرسي من نور حملة العرش. كذا في المطالب الوفية.
كل منهما (حق) ثابت بالآيات القرآنية والأحاديث النبوية؛ قال تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ رَبُّ الْعَرْشِ الْعَظِيمِ﴾ [سورة التوبة آية: ١٢٩]، وقال تعالى: ﴿وَسِعَ كُرْسِيُّهُ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ﴾ [سورة البقرة آية: ٢٥٥]، وقد مر من الأحاديث ما فيه الكفاية.
The Kursi is like the ring in the desert? And Ibn Jarir narrated from al-Dahhak: the Kursi is what is placed under the Throne upon which kings place their feet. And al-Firyabi, Ibn al-Mundhir, Ibn Abi Hatim, and al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak, and he authenticated it on the condition of the two Shaykhs, from Ibn Abbas: he said: the Kursi is the place of the two feet, and the Throne none can measure its magnitude. Thus mentioned al-Laqqani. And in Rashf al-Nasa'ih of al-Suhrawardi, may Allah have mercy on him, he said: Among what has been reported of the awesome power of Allah Most High and His creation before which minds are humbled and understandings vanish in describing the Kursi: Allah says: "His Kursi extends over the heavens and the earth" [Surah al-Baqara 2:255] – it is reported that each pillar of the Kursi is as long as the seven heavens and the seven earths, and it is before the Throne; and the Kursi is carried by four angels, each angel having four faces, their feet on the rock which is beneath the seventh lowest earth, five hundred years; an angel in the form of the master of humans, Adam, peace be upon him, who asks for provision and rain for the humans from year to year; an angel in the form of the master of cattle, the bull, who asks for provision for cattle from year to year; an angel in the form of the master of beasts of prey, the lion, who asks for provision for beasts of prey from year to year; an angel in the form of the master of birds, the eagle, who asks for provision for birds from year to year. And from Abu Idris al-Khawlani from Abu Dharr: he said: I said: O Messenger of Allah, which verse revealed to you is greatest? He said: "Ayat al-Kursi", then he said: "O Abu Dharr, the seven heavens compared to the Kursi are nothing but a ring thrown in a desert, and the superiority of the Throne over the Kursi is like the superiority of the desert over that ring." And in some reports: between the bearers of the Throne and the bearers of the Kursi are seventy veils of darkness and seventy veils of light, the thickness of each veil is a journey of five hundred years; and were it not for that, the bearers of the Kursi would be burnt by the light of the bearers of the Throne. Thus in al-Matalib al-Wafiyya. Each of them is true, established by Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths; He said: "And He is the Lord of the Mighty Throne" [Surah al-Tawba 9:129], and He said: "His Kursi extends over the heavens and the earth" [Surah al-Baqara 2:255], and sufficient hadiths have already been mentioned.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the Kursi (Footstool) of Allah and its relationship to the Throne (Arsh). The author begins by quoting a report from al-Dahhak that the Kursi is positioned under the Throne, similar to how kings place their feet on a footstool. He then cites Ibn Abbas through several chains that the Kursi is the place of the feet (of Allah in a manner befitting Him) and that no one can measure the Throne. The author then brings a lengthy description from al-Suhrawardi's work: the Kursi is so vast that each of its pillars spans the seven heavens and earths, and it is carried by four angels with four faces each, their feet on a rock five hundred years beneath the lowest earth. These angels are depicted in forms representing humans, cattle, beasts, and birds, each petitioning for provision for their respective types. The author then narrates the famous hadith of Abu Dharr where the Prophet, upon being asked about the greatest verse, said it was Ayat al-Kursi, and then gave the analogy: the seven heavens compared to the Kursi are like a ring in a desert, and the Throne's superiority over the Kursi is like that desert over the ring. Additional reports mention seventy veils of light and darkness between the bearers of the Throne and the bearers of the Kursi, each veil five hundred years thick, to prevent the bearers of the Kursi from being burnt. The passage concludes by affirming that both the Throne and the Kursi are absolutely true as established by the Quran (verses from al-Tawba and al-Baqara) and the hadiths already cited.

Key Terms
الكرسي
العرش
حملة العرش
آية الكرسي
الحلقة
الفلاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Kursi is equal to or greater than the Throne.
Correction: The hadith clarifies that the Throne is far greater: the heavens compared to the Kursi are like a ring in a desert, and the Throne's superiority over the Kursi is like the desert over that ring.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Abu Dharr, what is the relationship between the heavens, the Kursi, and the Throne?
A) The heavens are greater than the Kursi, and the Kursi is greater than the Throne.
B) The heavens compared to the Kursi are like a ring in a desert, and the Throne is even greater than the Kursi.
C) The Kursi is equal to the Throne in size.
D) The Throne is smaller than the Kursi.

Key Takeaway
The Kursi is a magnificent creation of Allah, yet it is incomparably smaller than the Throne, highlighting the limitless greatness of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are consumed by your worldly worries, do you pause to remember that Allah's Kursi encompasses the heavens and the earth, and that your problem is smaller than a speck before His infinite majesty? What practical step can you take today to remind yourself of His greatness when anxiety strikes?
?
The four angels tirelessly ask provision for every creature every year. Are you truly convinced that your rizq comes solely from Allah, or do you still rely on your own plans and efforts? Will you sincerely supplicate to Him tonight as the sole Provider, trusting Him to give you what is best?
?
If even the bearers of the Kursi would be burnt by the light of the bearers of the Throne, how far are you from truly knowing Allah's awe? Does this realization change how you approach your prayers and your awareness of His presence? Name one specific way you will cultivate khushu‘ (humility) in your worship starting today.

The Immensity of the Kursi
The author quotes the Quranic verse and a report about the Kursi's dimensions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic description of the Kursi and its vast dimensions that surpass human comprehension.

Core Idea
The Kursi, vast enough to encompass heavens and earth, is beyond human perception.

The author begins by stating that the human intellect cannot fully grasp the description of the Kursi. He then quotes the famous verse from Surah al-Baqarah and reports a tradition about the immense size of its legs. This lesson sets the stage for appreciating the majesty of this creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to get the overall claim about the Kursi's incomprehensibility and the verse.
2
Understand the verse
Reflect on the Quranic verse 'His Kursi extends over the heavens and the earth' and its implications.
This verse shows the Kursi encompasses all creation.
3
Ponder the reported size
Consider the tradition that each leg of the Kursi is as long as the seven heavens and earths, indicating its unimaginable scale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دون إدراكه العقول وتتلاشى الأفهام في وصف الكرسي يقول الله تعالى: ﴿وَسِعَ كُرْسِيُّهُ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ﴾ [سورة البقرة آية: ٢٥٥] - ورد أن كل قائمة من الكرسي طولها مثل السموات السبع والأرضين السبع، وهو بين يدي العرش ويحمل الكرسي بأربعة أملاك لكل ملك أربعة وجوه أقدامهم في الصخرة التي تحت الأرض السابعة السفلى خمسمائة عام، ملك على صورة سيد البشر آدم عليه السلام وهو يسأل للآدميين الرزق والمطر من السنة إلى السنة، وملك على صورة سيد الأنعام وهو الثور يسأل للأنعام الرزق من السنة إلى السنة، وملك على صورة سيد السباع وهو الأسد يسأل للسباع الرزق من السنة إلى السنة، وملك على صورة سيد الطير وهو النسر يسأل للطير الرزق من السنة إلى السنة، وعن أبي إدريس الخولاني عن أبي ذر قال: قلت: يا رسول الله أي آية نزل عليك أعظم؟ قال: «آيَةُ الكُرْسِيّ»، ثم قال: «يَا أَبَا ذَر مَا السَّمَوَاتُ السَّبْعُ مَعَ الكُرْسِيِّ إِلَّا كَحَلْقَةٍ مُلْقَاةٍ بِأَرْضِ فَلَاةٍ وَفَضْلُ العَرْشِ عَلَى الكُرْسِيِّ كَفَضْلِ الفَلَاةِ عَلَى الحَلْقَةِ» (١)، وفي بعض الأخبار: إن بين حملة العرش وحملة الكرسي سبعون حجابًا من ظلمة وسبعون حجابًا من نور، غلظ كل حجاب مسيرة خمسمائة سنة؛ ولولا ذلك لاحترقت حملة الكرسي من نور حملة العرش. كذا في المطالب الوفية.
Without the minds perceiving it and intellects dissipating in describing the Kursi. Allah the Exalted says: {His Kursi extends over the heavens and the earth} [Surah al-Baqarah: 255]. It is reported that each leg of the Kursi is of a length equal to the seven heavens and the seven earths, and it is between the hands of the Throne. The Kursi is carried by four angels, each angel having four faces; their feet are on the rock that is beneath the seventh lower earth, a distance of five hundred years. An angel in the form of the master of mankind, Adam (peace be upon him), who asks for the humans sustenance and rain from year to year. An angel in the form of the master of cattle, the bull, who asks for the cattle sustenance from year to year. An angel in the form of the master of beasts, the lion, who asks for the beasts sustenance from year to year. An angel in the form of the master of birds, the eagle, who asks for the birds sustenance from year to year. And from Abu Idris al-Khawlani from Abu Dharr, he said: I said: O Messenger of Allah, which verse was revealed to you that is greatest? He said: 'The Ayat al-Kursi.' Then he said: 'O Abu Dharr, the seven heavens compared to the Kursi are but like a ring thrown in a vast desert; and the superiority of the Throne over the Kursi is like the superiority of that desert over the ring.' And in some reports: Between the bearers of the Throne and the bearers of the Kursi are seventy veils of darkness and seventy veils of light, the thickness of each veil is a journey of five hundred years; and were it not for that, the bearers of the Kursi would be burnt by the light of the bearers of the Throne. As recorded in al-Matalib al-Wafiyyah.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a detailed description of the Kursi (Footstool) and its bearers, along with a hadith highlighting its relative size. The author begins by noting that the minds cannot fully grasp the description of the Kursi, indicating its grandeur. He then quotes the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:255) that the Kursi encompasses the heavens and the earth. He reports that each leg of the Kursi is as long as the seven heavens and earths combined, and it is located before the Throne. The Kursi is carried by four angels, each with four faces, and their feet are on a rock beneath the seventh earth, a distance of 500 years. Each angel has a specific form (human, bull, lion, eagle) and petitions for sustenance for their respective domains. Then he narrates a hadith from Abu Dharr where the Prophet declares Ayat al-Kursi the greatest verse and compares the heavens to a ring in a desert relative to the Kursi, and the Throne’s superiority to the Kursi as the desert is to the ring. Additional reports mention seventy veils of light and darkness between the bearers of the Throne and Kursi, preventing the latter from being burned by the former’s light. This underscores the immense scale of these creations and the glory of their Creator.

Key Terms
الكرسي
آية الكرسي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Kursi is only metaphorical or small in size.
Correction: This passage shows it is a immense real creation that encompasses the heavens and earth.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the length of each leg of the Kursi?
A) The distance between east and west
B) Equal to the seven heavens and seven earths
C) Five hundred years
D) Unknown

Key Takeaway
The Kursi is a real, vast creation that encompasses the heavens and the earth, demonstrating Allah's infinite majesty.

?

?

?
If the Kursi is such a magnificent creation, what does that tell you about the Creator? How will you change your attitude in prayer or daily life because of this realization?

The Four Angels Bearing the Kursi
The author describes the four angels carrying the Kursi, their forms, and their intercession for sustenance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know about the four angels who carry the Kursi, their forms, and their roles in sustaining creation.

Core Idea
Four unique angels, each overseeing a realm, bear the Kursi and intercede for sustenance.

After describing the vastness of the Kursi, the author introduces the four angels that carry it. Each angel has a distinct form and responsibility, petitioning Allah for the provision of different classes of creatures. This lesson reveals the intricate order in the unseen world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to identify the four angels and their assigned domains.
2
Notice the forms
Each angel is in the form of the 'master' of a category: human, cattle, beasts, birds. Think about the symbolism.
Adam for humans, bull for cattle, lion for beasts, eagle for birds.
3
Understand their function
They ask for sustenance and rain for their respective groups from year to year, showing the system of provision.

The Greatness of Ayat al-Kursi and the Throne
The author narrates a hadith about Ayat al-Kursi and additional reports about veils between the Throne and Kursi bearers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith comparing the heavens, Kursi, and Throne, and the veils between their bearers.

Core Idea
The Throne's superiority over the Kursi is like a desert over a ring; veils of light separate their bearers.

This lesson concludes the discussion with a powerful hadith narrated by Abu Dharr. The Prophet declares Ayat al-Kursi the greatest verse and gives a striking analogy for the relative sizes of the heavens, Kursi, and Throne. Additional reports describe the veils that protect the bearers of the Kursi from the overwhelming light of the Throne's bearers.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith

2
Analyze the analogy

3
Consider the veils
The additional report describes seventy veils each of darkness and light, each 500 years thick, protecting the Kursi bearers.

?

?

What veil (distraction, sin, forgetfulness) do you need to remove—or at least recognize—to stand before Him with the awe He deserves?
?
You have just learned that Ayat al-Kursi is the greatest verse. Are you treating it as such in your daily life? When was the last time you recited it with full awareness of the staggering reality it describes, and what change would it make if you did so every single night with that understanding?

beginner
4 min
Affirmation of the Throne and Kursi
The author affirms both the Throne and the Kursi are established by Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Throne and Kursi are real, literal entities affirmed by the Quran and hadith, not mere metaphors.

Core Idea
The Throne and Kursi are literal, true realities established by revelation.

This lesson addresses a key matter of 'aqidah: the reality of the Throne ('Arsh) and the Footstool (Kursi). The author asserts they are true, supported by explicit Quranic verses and prophetic traditions, countering any tendency to allegorize them. Understanding this affirms a core Sunni creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the directness of the affirmation: "Both of them are truth, established by Quranic verses and prophetic hadith."
The word 'truth' (ḥaqq) denotes certain reality.
2
Examine the Quranic proofs
The author cites two verses: one calling Allah the Lord of the Mighty Throne, and another describing the Kursi encompassing the heavens and earth. Reflect on how these verses establish the existence and attributes of these creations.
3
Understand the doctrinal significance
In Sunni creed, affirming the Throne and Kursi as real is obligatory. This passage counters those who interpret them metaphorically. Accepting them is part of iman in the ghayb (unseen).
This ties into the broader topic of sifat khabariyyah (reported attributes).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل منهما حق ثابت بالآيات القرآنية والأحاديث النبوية؛ قال تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ رَبُّ الْعَرْشِ الْعَظِيمِ﴾ [سورة التوبة آية: ١٢٩]، وقال تعالى: ﴿وَسِعَ كُرْسِيُّهُ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ﴾ [سورة البقرة آية: ٢٥٥]، وقد مر من الأحاديث ما فيه الكفاية.
Both of them (the Throne and the Kursi) are truth, established by Quranic verses and prophetic hadith. Allah the Exalted says: {And He is the Lord of the Mighty Throne} [Surah al-Tawbah: 129], and He says: {His Kursi extends over the heavens and the earth} [Surah al-Baqarah: 255]. And there have passed from the hadiths that which is sufficient.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This short passage serves as a doctrinal affirmation that both the 'Arsh (Throne) and the Kursi (Footstool) are true realities, not mere metaphors or symbols. The author states that they are established (thābit) by clear Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths. He cites two verses: one from Surah al-Tawbah (9:129) referring to Allah as the Lord of the Mighty Throne, and one from Surah al-Baqarah (2:255) stating that the Kursi encompasses the heavens and earth. He then notes that sufficient hadiths have already been mentioned in the preceding discourse (referring to the hadith about Ayat al-Kursi and other narrations). This reinforces the creedal position that believers must affirm these unseen realities as true and part of the ghayb (unseen) that is accepted from revelation.

Key Terms
العرش (al-‘Arsh)
الكرسي (al-Kursi)
آيات قرآنية (Quranic verses)
أحاديث نبوية (prophetic hadiths)
حق (truth)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Throne and Kursi are not real but are allegories for divine dominion or power.
Correction: The passage asserts that both are 'truth' (ḥaqq) and 'established' by revelation, meaning they are real creations, not metaphors.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the Throne and the Kursi?
A) They are both metaphorical.
B) They are both true, established by Quran and hadith.
C) Only the Throne is true.
D) They are both denied by scholars.

Key Takeaway
The Throne and Kursi are undeniable truths of revelation that every Muslim must affirm as real entities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe with certainty that the Throne and Kursi are real, physical creations, or have you ever allowed doubts about their literal existence to creep into your heart? What practical step can you take today to strengthen your conviction in this unseen reality?
?
The author says that 'sufficient hadiths' have already been presented. Have you ever personally sought out those hadiths to deepen your faith? What is holding you back from learning more about the very throne of your Lord?
?
When you recite Ayat al-Kursi, do you consciously remember that the Kursi is a real creation spanning the heavens and earth? How does that awareness change the way you recite and the awe you feel for Allah? If not, what will you do to cultivate that awareness starting from your next recitation?

Belief in Angels, Prophets, and Revealed Books
Tahawi enumerates three categories of belief in the unseen and adds a testimony of truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core Sunni belief in the existence and honor of angels, prophets, and revealed books, and the affirmation that they are upon clear truth and protected from sin.

Core Idea
The unseen realities are essential articles of faith, and the prophets are sinless.

This lesson covers the fundamental samiyyat (unseen matters) that every Muslim must believe. Imam Tahawi affirms belief in the honored angels, all prophets and messengers, and all revealed books. The commentary emphasizes that the prophets are protected from anything that would diminish their high rank.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the matn and commentary regarding angels, prophets, and books.
2
Identify the three categories
Notice that belief in angels, prophets, and books are listed separately; each is essential.
Angels are 'honored', prophets are 'all', books are 'sent down upon messengers'.
3
Understand prophetic infallibility
The commentary states prophets are 'ma'sumun' (protected) from all that would lower their rank. Reflect on why this is important.
This guards against the view that prophets could commit major sins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالملائكة والنبيين والكتب والكلام في أهل القبلة وَنُؤْمِنُ بِالمَلائِكَةِ وَالنَّبِيِّينَ وَالكُتُبِ المُنَزَّلَةِ عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ، وَنَشْهَدُ أَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا عَلَى الحَقِّ المُبِينِ، وَنُسَمِّي أَهْلَ قِبْلَتِنَا مُسْلِمِينَ مُؤْمِنِينَ مَا دَامُوا بِمَا جَاءَ بِهِ النَّبِيُّ عَلَيهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ مُعْتَرِفِينَ وَلَهُ بِكُلِّ مَا قَالَ وَأَخْبَرَ مُصَدِّقِينَ غَيْرَ مُكَذِّبِينَ. (ونؤمن بالملائكة) المكرمين (و) بجميع النبيين والمرسلين (و) بجميع الكتب المنزلة على الأنبياء (المرسلين) صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم أجمعين ونشهد أنهم كلهم كانوا على الحق المبين، وعن جميع ما يؤدي إلى نقص مراتبهم العلية معصومين. (ونسمي أهل قبلتنا) وهم الذين شهدوا شهادتنا واستقبلوا قبلتنا وصلوا صلاتنا وأكلوا ذبيحتنا (مسلمين) و (مؤمنين) وإن وصفوا بارتكاب الكبائر فاسقين (ما داموا) أي مدة دوامهم (بما) أي بالذي جاء به النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام معترفين اوله بكل ما قال وأخبر به (مصدقين) جازمين به (غير مكذبين)؛ ففي صحيح البخاري عن أنس بن مالك قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من صلى صلاتنا واستقبل قبلتنا وأكل ذبيحتنا فذلك المسلم الذي له ذمة الله وذمة رسوله فلا تخفروا الله في ذمته، وفيه عن أنس قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: أمرت أن أقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله فإذا قالوها وصلوا صلاتنا واستقبلوا قبلتنا وذبحوا ذبيحتنا فقد حرمت علينا دماؤهم وأموالهم إلا بحقها وحسابهم على الله.
Belief in angels, prophets, books, and the speech concerning the people of the qibla. And we believe in the honored angels, and in all the prophets and messengers, and in all the books sent down upon the messengers. And we testify that they were all upon the clear truth. And we call the people of our qibla 'Muslims' and 'believers' as long as they acknowledge what the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) brought and affirm everything he said and informed, without denial. (And we believe in the angels) the honored ones, (and) all the prophets and messengers, (and) all the books sent down upon the (messenger) prophets, blessings and peace of Allah be upon them all, and we testify that they were all upon the clear truth, and they are protected from everything that leads to deficiency in their exalted ranks. (And we call the people of our qibla) who are those who witness our testimony, face our qibla, pray our prayer, and eat our slaughtered meat (Muslims) and (believers) even if they are described as committing major sins and are sinners (as long as they) i.e., as long as they are (with what) i.e., with what the Prophet came with, acknowledging him and (affirming) everything he said and informed, being certain of it, (not denying). For in Sahih al-Bukhari from Anas ibn Malik, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever prays our prayer, faces our qibla, and eats our slaughtered meat, then that is the Muslim who has the protection of Allah and the protection of His Messenger, so do not violate Allah's covenant regarding his protection.' And in it from Anas, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'I have been commanded to fight the people until they say: There is no god but Allah. When they say it, pray our prayer, face our qibla, and sacrifice as we sacrifice, then their blood and wealth are forbidden to us except by its due, and their reckoning is with Allah.'
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a creedal statement and its commentary. It begins with the section heading: 'Belief in angels, prophets, books, and the speech concerning the people of the qibla.' Then the matn of Imam Tahawi states the core beliefs: belief in angels, prophets, and revealed books, and testimony that they were upon clear truth. It then defines who is called a Muslim or believer: those who acknowledge what the Prophet brought and affirm his every word and report, without denial. The commentary (sharh) then explains each phrase: 'we believe in the angels' specifies the honored ones; 'all prophets and messengers' includes all; 'all books' are those sent down; the prophets are protected from sin. For the ruling on people of the qibla, it explains that they are those who share the same testimony, face the same qibla, pray the same prayer, and eat halal meat. They are called Muslims and believers even if they commit major sins and are described as sinners, as long as they maintain acknowledgment and affirmation. Finally, it supports this with two hadiths from Sahih al-Bukhari: the first states that whoever prays our prayer, faces our qibla, and eats our slaughtered meat is a Muslim with the protection of Allah and His Messenger; the second states that the Prophet was commanded to fight people until they testify to tawhid, and when they do so and also perform these outward practices, their lives and property are sacred and their reckoning is with Allah. This demonstrates that outward adherence to the basic practices of Islam is the criterion for societal membership, while inner faith is left to Allah.

Key Terms
الملائكة
النبيين
الكتب المنزلة
المرسلين
معصومين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets could commit major sins like ordinary people.
Correction: The passage asserts the prophets are protected (معصومين) from all that would diminish their rank, affirming their infallibility.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the prophets regarding their ranks?
A) They were fallible and could commit sins.
B) They were protected from all that would lower their high rank.
C) They were only protected from minor sins.
D) The passage does not mention their protection.

Key Takeaway
Belief in angels, prophets, and books is foundational, and prophets are sinlessly protected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if angels are recording your deeds every moment, or do you sometimes forget they are present? What would change if you remembered them constantly?
?
When you read about the prophets, do you fully accept their absolute truthfulness, or do you entertain doubts about any part of their message? What does that reveal about your faith?
?
The passage says prophets are protected from anything that lowers their rank. Do you treat their teachings with the same reverence, or do you selectively follow them? Where is your heart falling short?

Who Is Called a Muslim? The Ruling on People of the Qibla
Tahawi defines the criteria for calling someone a Muslim and cites hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the criteria for calling someone a Muslim or believer according to Sunni Islam, and that committing major sins does not expel them from the fold of faith.

Core Idea
Outward practices qualify someone as Muslim; inner faith is left to Allah.

This lesson addresses a practical question: how do we identify a Muslim? Imam Tahawi states that we call those who share our qibla Muslims and believers, even if they commit major sins, as long as they acknowledge and affirm the Prophet's message. The commentary and hadiths from Bukhari reinforce that outward adherence to prayer, qibla, and zabiha are the markers of communal belonging.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the ruling on people of the qibla.
2
Identify the criteria
Note the list: sharing testimony, qibla, prayer, and food. Also see that committing major sins doesn't negate the status.
The phrase 'even if they are described as committing major sins' is key.
3
Study the hadith evidence
The two hadiths from Bukhari show that these outward signs determine protection of life and property.
The second hadith mentions fighting until they say la ilaha illa Allah and perform these practices.

Unseen Matters

All Revealed and Prophetic Reports Are True
The author affirms the truth of all Quranic and prophetic reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that both the Qur'an and authentic prophetic traditions are equally true and must be accepted with submission and certainty.

Core Idea
Every word of the Qur'an and authentic hadith is absolute truth.

In this lesson, we read a powerful affirmation from Imam al-Tahawi. He addresses a point of disagreement with al-Ash'ari and firmly states that everything Allah has revealed in the Qur'an—about the past, future, and the Hereafter—as well as everything authentically reported from the Prophet, is true. This includes the realities of the Sirat, the Mizan, Paradise, and Hellfire. The lesson emphasizes that this truth must be received with complete submission and unwavering certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal English translation. Let the author's own words settle in your mind.
Pay attention to the tone: it is a firm declaration.
2
Identify the two categories of reports
The passage mentions two sources: everything revealed in the Qur'an, and everything authentically reported from the Prophet. Note that both are declared 'true and correct'.
3
Note the specific examples given
The author lists the Sirat, Mizan, Jannah, and Nar as examples of what the Qur'an reports about the Hereafter. These are concrete realities that must be believed.
These are sam'iyyat (matters known only through revelation).
4
Reflect on the phrase 'bi-idh'ān wa īqān'
The passage ends with 'with submission and certainty'. Think about why the author emphasizes both intellectual acceptance and heartfelt surrender.
Submission (idh'ān) is the act of yielding, while certainty (īqān) is firm, unwavering knowledge.
5
Consider the context of disagreement
The author notes this is one of three issues where al-Tahawi differed from al-Ash'ari. Reflect on the importance of affirming the truth of all prophetic reports in the face of theological debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقول: وهذه إحدى المسائل الثلاث التي ذكر السبكي أن المصنف خالف فيها الأشعري). (و) نقول: (إن جميع ما أنزل الله تعالى (في القرآن) من الإخبار عما سلف ويكون في الأزمان وأحوال الآخرة من الصراط والميزان والجنان والنيران (و) كذلك (جميع ما صح عن النبي من الشرع والبيان كله حق وصدق بإذعان وإيقان.
I say: This is one of the three issues that al-Subki mentioned that the author disagreed with al-Ash'ari on. And we say: Indeed all that Allah the Exalted revealed (in the Qur'an) of reports about what has passed and what will be in the times and states of the Hereafter of the Sirat, the Scale, Paradise, and Fire, and likewise all that is authentically reported from the Prophet of the Shariah and exposition — all of it is true and correct with submission and certainty.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation. The author first identifies that he is addressing one of three issues where al-Tahawi reportedly differed with al-Ash'ari. He then states the correct position: everything Allah revealed in the Qur'an about the past, the future, and the conditions of the Hereafter — including the Sirat (bridge), the Mizan (scale), Jannah (Paradise), and Nar (Hellfire) — as well as all authentic prophetic teachings and explanations, is absolutely true and correct. The author stresses that this belief must be held 'bi-idh'ān wa īqān' (with submission and certainty), indicating that intellectual acceptance alone is insufficient; the heart must surrender and be firmly convinced.

Key Terms
الصراط
الميزان
الجنان
النيران
الإذعان
الإيقان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that only the Qur'an is authoritative and that prophetic hadiths are less authoritative or not necessarily true.
Correction: The author affirms that both Qur'anic reports and authentic prophetic traditions are equally true and must be accepted with submission and certainty.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must be accepted as true and correct?
A) Only the Qur'anic reports about the Hereafter
B) All Qur'anic reports and authentic prophetic traditions
C) Only the reports about the Sirat and Mizan
D) Only what is agreeable to reason

Key Takeaway
All authentic divine and prophetic reports are true and must be accepted with submission and certainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about the Sirat or the Scale, does your heart submit with certainty (īqān), or do you only nod intellectually? What is one specific report about the Hereafter that you find yourself doubting or dismissing? Today, write it down and pray for Allah to grant you sincere submission.
?

Belief in the Last Day and Resurrection
Definition of the Last Day and analysis of its relationship with resurrection after death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the Last Day as per the commentator and the grammatical relationship between 'Last Day' and 'resurrection after death'.

Core Idea
The Last Day spans from death to judgment; resurrection is either a confirmation or a specific instance.

This lesson examines the fifth pillar of faith in the Tahaawiyyah: belief in the Last Day and the resurrection after death. The commentator carefully defines the scope of the Last Day and then clarifies how the phrase 'resurrection after death' relates to it. This is a classic example of how kalam texts use grammatical analysis to expound doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own wording come through.
2
Define the Last Day
Notice how the commentator defines the Last Day: from death to the end of what happens on the Day of Resurrection. It is called 'last' because it is the final limited day.
3
Analyze the two possibilities
The commentator gives two possibilities for the phrase 'resurrection after death': it is either a confirmation (ta'kid) of the Last Day, or a conjunction of the specific (resurrection) to the general (Last Day).
Think about how these two interpretations affect the overall meaning.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the commentator mentions both possibilities. This shows the precision of theological language and the importance of understanding the relationship between terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاليَوْمِ الْآخِرِ) وهو من الموت إلى آخر ما يقع يوم القيامة؛ وصف بذلك لأنه آخر يوم محدود، وقوله : ( وَالْبَعْثِ بَعْدَ المَوْتِ) إما تأكيد لليوم الآخر وإما من عطف الخاص على العام.

Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This brief passage explains the fifth pillar: belief in the Last Day (al-yawm al-akhir) and the resurrection after death (al-ba'th ba'd al-mawt). The commentator defines the Last Day as stretching from the moment of death to the end of all events of the Day of Judgment. It is called 'last' because it is the final of the limited days. Then the commentator addresses the relationship between the two phrases in the matn: 'al-ba'th ba'd al-mawt' could be an emphatic restatement of 'al-yawm al-akhir' or a specific instance (resurrection) subsumed under the general term (Last Day). This is a common grammatical analysis in kalam texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

C) 'al-yawm' is a metaphor for 'al-ba'th'

Key Takeaway
The Last Day in the Tahaawiyyah includes the entire period from death to the final judgment, and resurrection after death is either an emphasis or a specific component of it.

The Last Day and Resurrection
Imam Maydani defines the Last Day and discusses the phrase 'resurrection after death'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the Last Day and the two possible interpretations of 'resurrection after death' as either an emphasis or a specification.

Core Idea
The Last Day spans from death to the final events of the Day of Resurrection.

In this passage, Imam Maydani clarifies what is meant by 'the Last Day' and how the phrase 'resurrection after death' relates to it. Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping the Islamic eschatological timeline.

Imam Maydani states that 'resurrection after death' is either a تأكيد (emphasis) of the Last Day or a عطف الخاص على العام (specification of the general). Consider how each interpretation affects the meaning.
The first interpretation makes resurrection synonymous with the Last Day; the second makes it a specific event within it.

This guards against the misconception that the Last Day is only the Day of Resurrection.

The Fate of Major Sinners from the Ummah
The author clarifies the ruling on major sinners: they are not eternally in Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunnah holds that monotheistic major sinners are not eternally punished in Hell and how divine justice and mercy are reconciled.

Core Idea
Major sins do not lead to eternal punishment as long as one dies with monotheism.

This lesson presents a foundational Sunni doctrine concerning the fate of believers who commit major sins. The passage clarifies that while such sinners may be punished, they are not condemned to eternal fire, balancing divine justice with mercy. It also provides Quranic and rational evidence for this position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note that the author states clearly that people of major sins from the Ummah will not be eternally in Hell if they die as monotheists.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا يُخَلَّدُونَ' — they will not be made eternal.
2
Reflect on the Quranic evidence
The author quotes Quran 4:48 to support the possibility of forgiveness for sins other than shirk. Consider how this verse underpins the argument.
3
Understand the reasoning based on divine justice
The passage explains that eternal punishment is reserved for disbelief (kufr). Since the sinners are monotheists, eternal punishment would be disproportionate, contradicting God's promise of justice.
This reasoning uses the principle that God does not break His promise (referenced in the commentary).
4
Consider the role of intercession
The passage mentions that after punishment, the sinners are brought out by mercy and intercession. Reflect on how this shows God's mercy.
Intercession is from the obedient people, including prophets and saints.

(و) نقول: (أهل الكبائر من أمة نبينا ( محمد ) وكذا جميع أمم الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام، وخصه بالذكر إما لاتفاق الحكم في جميع الأمم فإذا علم حكم أمته علم الحكم في جميع الأمم الماضية حيث كانوا كلهم جاءوا بالتوحيد، وإما لكونهم داخلين في حكم أمته حيث كان العهد مأخوذاً عليهم إن أدركوه ليؤمنن به فرسالته عامة لجميع الأمم، والحاصل أن جميع أهل الكبائر من أهل التوحيد إذا أراد الله تطهيرهم ( في النار لا يخلدون إذا ماتوا وهم موحدون وإن لم يكونوا تائبين بعد أن لقوا الله عارفين) أي معترفين له بالتوحيد وبه (مؤمنين) بلا ترديد؛ وذلك لأن التخليد في النار من أعظم العقوبات، وقد جعله الله جزاء الكفر الذي هو أعظم الجنايات؛ فلو جوزي به غير الكافر كان زيادة على قدر الجناية فيلزم منه خلف الوعد، وذلك لا يجوز عليه تعالى؛ قال تعالى: (إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يُخْلِفُ الْمِيعَادَ ﴾ [سورة آل عمران آية: 9]، قال العلامة
And the people of major sins from the nation of Muhammad will not remain eternally in the Fire when they die as monotheists even if they were not repentant, after they have met God as knowers and believers. And if He wills, He punishes them in the Fire according to the measure of their sin by His justice, then He brings them out of it by His mercy and the intercession of the intercessors from among His obedient people, then He sends them to His Paradise. The conclusion is that all people of major sins from the people of monotheism, if God wills to purify them, will not remain eternally in the Fire when they die as monotheists even if they were not repentant after they have met God as knowers, i.e., acknowledging His monotheism, and as believers without hesitation. That is because eternal punishment in the Fire is one of the greatest punishments, and God has made it the recompense of disbelief, which is the greatest of crimes. So if non-disbelievers were recompensed with it, it would be an increase beyond the measure of the crime, entailing a violation of the promise, and that is not permissible for Him, Exalted. He, Exalted, said: 'Indeed, Allah does not break His promise.' The scholar said:

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement followed by commentary. It first states the position of Ahl al-Sunnah regarding major sinners (أهل الكبائر): they will not be eternally in Hell as long as they die as monotheists, even if unrepentant. They are under God's will: He may forgive them by His grace or punish them justly and then bring them out through mercy and intercession. The passage quotes Quran 4:48 to show that shirk is unforgivable but lesser sins may be forgiven. It also mentions that the people of major sins are not like the deniers who are eternally lost. Then a prayer is included. The commentary then elaborates: the ruling applies to all nations of prophets, not just Muhammad's nation. It explains that eternal punishment (تخليد) is the penalty for kufr ( disbelief). If it were applied to non-disbelievers, it would exceed the crime and violate God's promise not to wrong anyone, citing Quran 3:9. Thus the passage concludes that monotheistic sinners cannot be eternally punished.

Justice, Mercy, and Intercession for Sinful Believers
Imam Maydani explains the fate of sinful believers: punishment, intercession, and final admission to Paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how sinful believers may be punished justly, then saved by Allah's mercy and intercession, and how this is supported by hadith.

Core Idea
Intercession follows just punishment, showing mercy without compromising justice.

This passage from Imam Maydani addresses a critical question: What happens to believers who die with sins? It explains that Allah, in His perfect justice, may punish them in Hell, but then in His vast mercy and through the intercession of prophets and righteous, He brings them out. The passage also provides hadith evidence and concludes with a humble supplication.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the sequence of ideas: punishment, mercy, intercession, hadith, supplication.
The passage includes embedded hadith references.
2
Identify the three key elements
Identify the three main doctrinal points: divine justice (punishment), divine mercy (bringing out of Hell), and intercession (by prophets, angels, believers).
Justice and mercy are not contradictory here.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The author cites two mutawatir hadiths. Note how the first shows the sequence of intercession, and the second promises a grand number entering Paradise through one man's intercession.
The hadiths are not fully quoted but referenced.
4
Reflect on the supplication
The passage ends with a supplication asking for steadfastness in Islam and divine pleasure. Consider why the author includes this personal prayer.
Supplication shows the author's humility and concern.
5
Reconcile justice and mercy
Think about how this passage resolves the apparent conflict between God's justice and mercy: punishment is by justice, then mercy intervenes after purification.
Intercession is by permission, not independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَانَ فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكَ عَظِيمًا ﴾ [سورة النساء آية: ١١٣) (وإن شاء عذبهم في النار المعدة لتطهير الأوزار (بقدر جنايتهم) وظلمهم لأنفسهم، وذلك (بعدله) وحكمته، ثم يخرجهم منها برحمته التي وسعت كل شيء من بريته (۱) وشفاعة الشافعين من أهل طاعته كأنبيائه ورسله وملائكته وأهل معرفته؛ وذلك بإذنه ومشيئته؛ للأحاديث الكثيرة المتواترة المعنى: منها حديث أبي سعيد في الصحيحين أن ناسا قالوا يا رسول الله هل نری ربنا يوم القيامة؟... الحديث بطوله وفيه: «فَيَقُولُ اللهُ تَعَالَى شَفَعَتِ المَلَائِكَةُ وَشَفَعَ النَّبِيُّونَ وَشَفَعَ المؤمِنُونَ وَلَمْ يَبْقَ إِلَّا أَرْحَمُ الرَّاحِمِينَ (٢). ومنها حديث الترمذي وابن ماجه وابن حبان وغيرهم: «لَيَدْخُلَنَّ الجنَّةَ بِشَفَاعَةِ رَجُلٍ مِنْ أُمَّتِي أَكْثَرُ مِنْ بَنِي غَمِيمٍ (۳).
